=245  \\$aTerpsichore:$bMasque, Consisting of a Prelude, Airs Duettes, a Chorus, and Dances
=250  \\$a1st ed.
=260  \\$aLondon$bArnold$c1795
=300  \\$a53 pages
=490  \\$aThe Works of G. F. Händel, Ed. in Score$v159-160
=500  \\$aTerpsicore is a prologue in the form of an opéra-ballet by George Frideric Handel. Handel composed it in 1734 for a revision of his opera Il pastor fido which had first been presented in 1712. The revision of Il pastor fido with Terpsicore as the prologue was first performed on 9 November 1734 at Covent Garden theatre in London, opening Handel's first season in that newly built theatre.
=500  \\$aIt is the only example of a Handel opera with a prologue, and is patterned on the similar extended prologues in the works of Jean-Philippe Rameau, blending operatic arias, choruses, and dancing. The work opens with a chorus, followed by a bravura aria each for Apollo and Erato. Terpsicore demonstrates the power of dance in a series of contrasted dance movements, interspersed with duets and solos from the singers.
=500  \\$aPages 47-53 include dances and two arias from other operas: 'Arianna' and 'Flavio'.
=500  \\$athe incipits don't entirely match those in the Händel-Handbuch

=245  \\$aLitanies à la Vierge :$bNoire Notre-Dame de Roc-Amadour pour chœur de femmes ou d'enfants à 3 parties avec accompagnement d'orgue
=250  \\$a1st ed.
=260  \\$aParis$bDurand$c1937
=300  \\$a15 pages
=500  \\$aLitanies à la Vierge noire ("Litany to the Black Virgin"), FP 82, is a piece of sacred music composed in 1936 for a three-part choir of women (or children) and organ, setting a French litany recited at the pilgrimage site Rocamadour which the composer visited. The subtitle, Notre-Dame de Rocamadour, refers to the venerated black sculpture of Mary. The composition is Poulenc's first piece of sacred music. In 1947 he wrote a version for voices accompanied by string orchestra and timpani. 
=500  \\$aAutograph of Poulenc and dedication to a friend on the first page, dated 1937

=245  \\$aAccessiones historiæ Anhaltinæ$bVon unterschiedenen Das Hoch-Fürstl. Hauß Und Fürstenthum Anhalt Belangenden Materien sampt dazu gehörigen Documenten
=250  \\$a1st ed.
=260  \\$aZerbst$bZimmermann$c1716
=300  \\$a[vi]-632-[7] pages$bplates, folded pages
=500  \\$aBeckmann was a German university professor, librarian and historian. He taught Greek, history, politics and theology at the Brandenburg University of Frankfurt and was the university's rector for many years. Bekmann published numerous works in various fields. His alphabetical catalogue of the Frankfurt University Library, published in 1676, which was an innovation at the time, became significant. He also earned lasting merit as a chronicler of the Anhaltinian principalities and the Mark Brandenburg.
=500  \\$aWith large fold-outs and pamphlets

=100  \\$aDussen, Jan Herman van der$4cmp$97625$d1805-1859
=245  \\$aDer engelenzang. $bDriestemmig in Muzijk gebragt, met accompagnement van het orgel of piano
=260  \\$aDelft$bBettenhausen$cs.d.
=300  \\$a14-[1] pages
=500  \\$aUnfindable work
=500  \\$a3-voice choral score with keyboard accompaniment
=500  \\$aJ. H. van der Dussen was a dutch Organist in the Bovenkerk in Kampen
=500  \\$aOn endpaper: "Geheel overeenkomstig met dit accompagnement is bij de vervaardiger van dezen Engelenzang insgelijks te bekomen, een afschrift van het Orkest accompagnement à 3 Gulden" (Fully in accordance with this accompaniment, a copy of the orchestral accompaniment at 3 Gulden is also available from the maker of this Engelenzang)
=504  \\$aVan der Dussen, who was born on 30 September 1782 in Arnhem as the son of the organist of the Grote Kerk there, was, before his appointment to Kampen, organist of the Lutheran Church in Arnhem and Kapellmeister of the Batavian Civic Guard Corps. At Kampen, he was also conductor of the choir. As city music master, he took care of the music college's rehearsals and concerts. Furthermore, he had to give music lessons, enliven promotions at the Latin school with a group of musicians, give public (organ) concerts and take care of everything related to the music college. Van der Dussen sometimes acted as inspector for repairing or building new organs, for instance in Elburg (1825), Terwolde (1827) and Heerde (1845). He also wrote about church music and composed. Van der Dussen married Johanna Geertruide Zegers. Of his children, Frederik followed in his father's footsteps. In 1855, the festive celebration of Jan Herman van der Dussen's 50th anniversary as organist in Kampen took place. He died on 15 February 1859.

=300  \\$a4 pages
=500  \\$aThe Music for the Royal Fireworks is a suite in D major (originally for wind instruments) composed by George Frideric Handel in 1749 under contract of George II of Great Britain for the fireworks in London's Green Park on 27 April 1749. The music celebrates the end of the War of the Austrian Succession and the signing of the Treaty of Aix-la-Chapelle (Aachen) in 1748.

=260  \\$aLondon$bSimpson$c[1744]
=300  \\$a22 pages$bmodern cardboard binding, leather spine and corners
=500  \\$aSignature by Havergal
=500  \\$aGroneman was a Dutch composer, violinist and organist and carillonneur of German descent.
=500  \\$aHis collections of sonatas for flute were published in London by the publisher Walsh; his trio sonatas were printed in Paris. Parts from a sonata for flute were included in the duets anthology Recueil de Pièces by French flutist Michel Blavet. Groneman's sonatas were composed in the so-called Empfindsame style and Galante style. The first sonatas still include four movements, while the later sonatas consist of the more modern three movements.

=041  \\$adut$alat
=100  \\$aZumbach von Coesfeld, Coenraad$d1697-1780$4aut$4asn$97275
=245  \\$a[39 manuscripts and pamphlets]
=260  \\$as.l.$c1730-1865
=300  \\$a140 pages
=500  \\$a39 manuscripts and some printed pamphlets by or about C. Zumbach von Coesveld, collected and written by J. T. Bodel Nijenhuis.
=500  \\$aConradus Zumbach von Coesfeld (1697-1780) was city doctor in Leiden. He published works on the Netherlands' struggle with the water, and collaborated on the development of a geometric sea instrument.
=500  \\$aNijenhuis was a Dutch publisher and map collector. He is the namesake of the very extensive Bodel Nijenhuis Collection (atlasses and maps) in the Leiden University Library.
=500  \\$aThe collector Bodel Nijenhuis compares Coesveld to J. Le Franq van Berkheij for his broad general knowledge and writings, and surprisingly many biographical details coincide. Very thorough biographical and bibliographical study. 
=500  \\$aVarious subjects, but no music
Contains:
C.ZUMBACH de KOESFELT, Korte schets om het schep, hef- of waterrad in de watermolens te verbeteren (...) tot groot voordeel van den (...) droogmakeryen voorgestelt, Leiden, 1770
DANKRYM aan den heere L(aurentius) S(tevensloot) (...) op C. Zumbag de Coesveld, 1730
J.T. BODEL NIJENHUIS, De Leidsche Medicinae Doctor Zumbag de Koesvelt, 1865 ( drafts of Zumbach de Coesfeld's biography)
Notes andcorrespondentie about Zumbach von Coesveld with/by Bodel Nijenhuis
Correspondence with Jacob de Rhoer and other members of Leiden university

=500  \\$aJoseph (also known as Joseph en Égypte) is an opéra mêlé de chant/opéra en prose in three acts by the French composer Étienne Méhul. The libretto, by Alexandre Duval, is based on the Biblical story of Joseph and his brothers. The work was first performed by the Opéra-Comique in Paris on 17 February 1807 at the Théâtre Feydeau.

=260  \\$aLyon$bde la Roche$c1787
=300  \\$a2 vols. in 1 (xxxvi-436+404 pages)$bmusical notation, 2 engraved frontispieces
=500  \\$aIn part 2 (p. 225 etc): musical notation and information on plainchant.
=520  \\$aAntoine de Montazet (17 August 1713-2 May 1788) was a French theologian, of Jansenist tendencies, who became bishop of Autun and archbishop of Lyon. He was elected to the Académie française in 1756. Contrary to the papal bull of Pope Pius V on the Roman Breviary, Montazet changed the text of the Breviary and the Missal. The later efforts of Pope Pius IX and Cardinal Bonald to suppress the innovations of Montazet provoked resistance on the part of the canons, who defended the traditional Lyonnese ceremonies (Wikipedia).

=500  \\$aIn the back, note in pensil "Strassburger Ex. im Jahre 1870 wohl verbrannt, daher ist diese Nachbildung dest(o) gesucht" ("Strasbourg copy probably burnt in 1870, therefore this replica is the more sought after")
=500  \\$aProtestantism in Strasbourg is an important aspect of the history and sociology of the city. The Protestant Reformation was introduced in Strasbourg as early as 1518, when Matthieu Zell preached in Strasbourg in the Lutheran manner. In 1520, Pierre-Philippe de Remiremont preached the Reformation in the church of Saint-Pierre-le-Vieux in Strasbourg. In 1524, the pastor Martin Bucer moved to the church of Sainte-Aurélie in Strasbourg, outside the walls of Old Strasbourg, and then 1531 to the church of Saint Thomas in Strasbourg. In 1529 the cathedral was given over to Protestant worship. The city officially joined Lutheranism in 1532.

=500  \\$aJohann Lauremberg, also Johannes Lauremberg, occasionally incorrect: Johann Wilhelm Laurenberg (* 26 February 1590 in Rostock; † 28 February 1658 in Sorø, Denmark) was a mathematician and cartographer as well as a Low German poet and writer of the Baroque period. As a pseudonym he used the name "Hans Willmsen L. Rost." (= Johann, son of Wilhelm Lauremberg Rostochiensis).

=500  \\$aA novena (from Latin: novem, "nine") is an ancient tradition of devotional praying in Christianity, consisting of private or public prayers repeated for nine successive days or weeks. The prayers are often derived from devotional prayer books, or consist of the recitation of the rosary (a "rosary novena"), or of short prayers through the day. Novena prayers are customarily printed in small booklets, and the novena is often dedicated to a specific angel, saint, Marian title of the Blessed Virgin Mary, or one of the persons of the Holy Trinity.
=500  \\$aAs the author Fr. Bernardo de Santa Maria Rosa was preacher and Master of Ceremonies of the Royal Convent of S. Francisco da Cidade do Porto, it could well be that this prayer/songbook was used at the Novenas for the Virgin in the liturgic rituals at the abbey mentioned. The feast day of the Virgin of the Immaculate Conception is 8 December.
=500  \\$aEngraved Frontispiece, iconography of the Virgin of the Immaculate Conception shows her standing, with arms outstretched or hands clasped in prayer.

=500  \\$aAntoine de Pas, Marquis de Feuquières (1648 - 1711) was a French writer and soldier, who served in the wars of Louis XIV. His "Mémoires de M. le Marquis de Feuquiere, lieutenant general des armées du roi: contenans les maximes sur la guerre, & l'application des exemples aux maximes" ran to 42 editions between 1736 and 2014 and was translated into three languages. Completed just before his death in 1711, it was highly critical of Louis XIV and remained unpublished until 1736. Voltaire later used it as a source for his own work, "Siècle de Louis XIV". 
=500  \\$a The book begins with a long biographical presentation of the marquis written by the abbot Gabriel Pérau to whom  we owe this edition. 
=500  \\$aParticularly comprehensive, it includes a good understanding of the importance that France had in the Thirty Years' War and the particularly fundamental role of the Marquis de Feuquières in the formation of the alliance against the House of Austria.

=041  \\$afre
=100  \\$aJoly, Claude$d1607-1700$4aut$97709
=245  \\$aRecueil de maximes véritables et importantes pour l'institution du Roy
=260  \\$aParis$bElsevier$c1653
=300  \\$a[xxii]-584-[2] pages$bgilded pages
=336  \\$abook
=336  \\$aprinted
=500  \\$aThe most prominent rebellions in the mid-seventeenth century France were those of the nobles and the judges and known as the 'Fronde'.The leading theoretician of the parleamentary fronde was Claude Joly. His treatise 'Recueil de maximes' is a collection of constitutionalist maxims, remnants of a pre-absolutist age, and include trenchant attacks on two contributions of Cardinals Richelieu and Mazarin to political thought and practice in France. One was the new motion that the king is rightly the master - in effect the owner - of the persons and properties of all inhabitants of France. The other was the Machiavellian view that succesful public policy requires the systematic use of immoral means. The King's power, warned Joly, is limited and not automatically sanctionned by divine law. Frenchmen posess just title to their lives and properties, and are not the slaves of a despot or tyrant. The king's original divine power is mediated through the French people, Joly added, and the king cannot rightfully tax the French without the consent of the states-general. The fact that Joly was reviled by the king and his party as a rebel and a traitor, he declared, shows that the old constitutionhas been overcome by new views holding the king to have unlimited authority above all law. For Joly this view was 'pure usurpation'  bred in the 'monstrous cauldron' of Machiavel.

=500  \\$aCharles Rollin (1661-1741) was a French historian and educator, very popular in his time. His literary work dates chiefly from the later years of his life, when he had been forbidden to teach. His once famous Ancient History (French: Histoire Ancienne, 12 vols., Paris, 1730–38) and the less generally read Roman History (Histoire Romaine, only five of nine volumes finished by the time of his death) were avowed compilations, uncritical and somewhat inaccurate. But they instructed and interested, generation after generation.

=590  \\$aNel quale si vede chiaro non sol'il vero, facile, e breve modo d'imparar di cantare di canto figurato e fermo Ma vi si vedon' anco dichiarate con bellissim'ordine tutte le principali materie, che ivi si trattano, sciolte le maggiori difficoltà, che all'incipienti, proficienti, e perfetti in essa occorrono, e scoperti nuovi segreti nella medesima circa il cantare, comporre, e sonar di tasti, nascoti. =245  \\$aCatalogus quorumdam librorum prostantium in officina viduæ Cornelii Verdussen & consortis Bibliopolæ Antverpiæ
=260  \\$aAntwerp$bs.n.$c17xx

=336  \\$abook
=336  \\$aprinted
=500  \\$aVerdussen was a dynasty of printers in Antwerp, starting with Hieronymus Verdussen I in the late sixteenth century, and ending around 1800. Many other printers in Antwerp were also related to the Verdussens through marriage. They specialized in religious works and works in Spanish,[1] but also published newspapers, almanachs, poetry, scientific works, .... By the end of the 17th century, they produced about 21% of the Spanish books printed in the Netherlands, and with 5 presses was second only to Moretus in Antwerp.

=100  \\$aBoer, Francijntje de$d1784-1852$4aut$1http://www.wikidata.org/entity/Q2299757$97737
=245  \\$aNieuwe dichtproeven$bvan Francijntje De Boer Dienstmaagd te Sneek

=336  \\$abook
=336  \\$aprinted
=500  \\$aContains some loose clippings - papercraft and illustrations from printed sources - as well as a handwritten leaflet notificating the death of Francijntje de Boer
=500  \\$aFrancijntje de Boer was a Dutch maid and writer of particularly successful children's poems. Between 1815 and 1825, she published four volumes of poetry, three of which were for children. Her language is characterised by simplicity. Her poems revolve around domesticity, virtue and pure religiousness. Despite her modest social position, she had contact with other Dutch female poets, including Fenna Mastenbroek, Petronella Moens and Anna Barbara van Meerten-Schilperoort. During her lifetime, she enjoyed widespread fame. A total of eight editions of her 'Gedichtjes voor kinderen' appeared until the end of 1870, and a French translation by Auguste Clavareau in 1835. The various printings varied in design and illustration, and were widely distributed, serving in schools as prizes for pupils or as teaching material.

=500  \\$aOriginally published in 1616
=500  \\$aLucelle is a true Romeo & Juliet adaptation by Bredero. A play that moved Maria Tesselschade to tears at the premiere in 1615, a play that was immortalised many times by painters such as Jan Steen and Jan Miense Moleaer, a play that was reprinted more than any of Bredero's plays in the 17th and 18th centuries, a play with the recognisable topical emotion of unattainable love due to a difference in descent.
=500  \\$aFinal scene of the play painted by Molenaer:
https://www.pubhist.com/w7503

=500  \\$aBredero signs the play with 'overgeset en gerijmt' (translated and put in rhymes), pointing herewith at the fact that this tragicomedy was based on a foreing template, namely the ‘tragi-comedie en prose ’ Lucelle (1576) by the French writer Louis Le Jars

=041  \\$adut
=245  \\$aEpitaphium, ofte graf-dicht op 't overlyden vanden sinrijcken Poeets G. A. Brederode
=260  \\$as.l.$bs.n.$cs.d.
=300  \\$a[14] pages
=500  \\$aElegies after the death of Bredero. 
=500  \\$aDigitized later edition at https://www.dbnl.org/tekst/stui002memo01_01/stui002memo01_01_0041.php
=500  \\$aOriginal title page (with portrait of Bredero) is missing (cut out?)
=500  \\$aThis edition of Elegies (Lijck-dichten) shows clearly the status of Bredero as a local celebrity at that very moment. Such a publication was unprecedented, and it demonstrates how popular the poet was among his fellow citizens. They all strongly and intensely experienced the loss. The elegies were written by different poets, including famous Dutch authors like Samuel Coster, Petrus Scriverius and Joost van den Vondel. It marks Bredero’s decease as a moment at which Amsterdam authors sing the praises of their popular and much-loved former colleague. The poems predominantly breathe the usual funeral topics of praise, grief and consolation. But the very first of all these poems, a lengthy `Epitaph, or elegy on the death of the significant poet G.A. Bredero’ (`Epitaphium. Oft Graf-dicht Op ’t overlyden vanden sinrijcken Poeet G.A. Brederood’), tells its readers how Bredero died a sudden death, (probably heart failure).

=520  \\$aIn 1678, Lorenzani traveled to Paris, hoping to find fortune. His motets were performed for Louis XIV, who recognized his talent and appointed him music master to the queen. Under orders of the king, Lorenzani traveled back to Italy and recruited singers for the monarch's chapel. Despite assistance from Madame de Montespan, he never achieved sufficient popularity to overcome great antagonism from Jean-Baptiste Lully.

=100  \\$aKöhler, Johann David$d1684-1755$4aut$1http://www.wikidata.org/entity/Q88653$97932
=245  \\$aSylloge aliquot scriptorum de bene ordinanda et ornanda Bibliotheca
=260  \\$aFrankfurt$bStein$c1728
=300  \\$a[x]-252 pages
=500  \\$aKöhler was a German historian, numismatist and heraldist. He served as university librarian at Altdorf (Nürnberg) and contributed substantially to early library science. The 1728 'Sylloge' is one of three monographs upon which Köhler's credentials as a library and information scientist are based upon. Though compiling older texts by Jean Garnier, Frederik Rostgaard, Giusto Fontanini, and Daniel Wilhelm Moller, it can be seen as one of the first anthologies of library classification, organization and cataloguing schemes.

=245  \\$aScanderberg.$bTragédie
=250  \\$a1st ed.
=260  \\$aParis$bFrancœur$bBoivin$bLe Clerc$c1735
=300  \\$a[ii]-246 pages
=500  \\$avocal score engraved by Mathieu Degland
=500  \\$aScanderberg is an opera by the French composers François Francoeur and François Rebel, first performed at the Académie Royale de Musique (the Paris Opera) on 27 October 1735. It takes the form of a tragédie en musique in a prologue and five acts. The libretto, by Antoine Houdar de La Motte and Jean-Louis-Ignace de La Serre, is based on the life of the Albanian patriot Skanderbeg, who led the resistance against the Ottoman Empire in the 15th century.

=100  \\$aBach, Johann Sebastian$d1685-1750$4cmp$1http://www.wikidata.org/entity/Q1339$94766
=240  \\$a6 Violin Sonatas BWV 1014-1019
=245  \\$aClavier Sonaten mit obligater Violine 
=250  \\$a1st ed.
=260  \\$aZürich$bNägeli$cs.d
=300  \\$a2 vols ([ii]-95+25 pages)$boblong
=500  \\$aHarpsichord and violin parts
=500  \\$afirst printed edition of the sonatas published by the Swiss musicologist Hans Georg Nägeli in Zurich in the early 1800s. The son of a musically inclined Protestant pastor in Wetzikon, Nägeli showed precocious musical skills. In 1790 he moved to Zurich where he took lessons with the Swiss pianist Johann David Brünings, who introduced him to the music of Bach. A year later he set up a music shop and in 1794 a publishing house. Corresponding with Bach's publisher Bernhard Christoph Breitkopf and the widow of C.P.E. Bach, he was able to acquire Bach manuscripts, including that of the Mass in B minor, which he eventually published. His Bach publications started with The Well-Tempered Clavier in 1801 and The Art of Fugue in 1802.

=500  \\$aHenry Holcombe was 'the boy' Prenesto in 'Camilla', one of the earliest Italian operas in London, and the page in Addison's 'Rosamond'. He left the stage when his voice broke, and became a successful teacher of singing and of the harpsichord to various families. He died around 1750 (according to Hawkins 1776, V, 187) or 1752.

=500  \\$aOnly two songs from a total of 9, from Ier Livre: I.Action de grâces, and from IIme Livre: V. L'Épouse.
=500  \\$aIn addition to Racine, some of the occupants of 24, rue Visconti [Paris] had a certain reputation. Among them, the trompe l'oeil painter Jacques Poirier but also the composer Guy-Bernard Delapierre (whose professional name was Guy Bernard), known for his film music and a ballet, "Algues", staged at the Paris Opera. This "charming man", who gave concerts in his home on the first floor, was also the author of the book "L'Art de la Musique", an art critic and an Egyptologist.
Guy-Bernard Delapierre had met Olivier Messiaen in German captivity at the end of 1940 and they met again in Paris in early 1943. Messiaen gave private composition lessons at his friend's home in Rue Visconti from autumn 1943 until 1947. In return, the host wrote several articles about the master in the post-war period, including "Souvenirs sur Olivier Messiaen" in 1945 in the Lausanne art journal "Formes et couleurs".
=501  \\$aLa Mort du nombre, Vocalise-étude pour voix élevées, Chants de terre et de ciel
=561  \\$aAutograph dedication by the composer: "à Guy Bernard Delapierre, en souvenir de ces quatre jours horribles et merveilleux. Tout à la fois, passé à Nancy, et d'inoubliables conversations musicales, littéraires, religieuses etc. etc. (car nous avions effleurés tants de sujets !) Et en toute affection, Olivier Messiaen, Marcelle Baulet, 28 février 1943"

=500  \\$aLuigi Antonio Sabbatini (1732-1809) was an Italian composer and music theorist. He studied music at Bologna in the Franciscan Monastery, under Father Giovanni Battista Martini. He published a textbook on the theoretical elements of music, in 1789, in three volumes, a treatise on fugues, in 1802. He also contributed to the use of numerical signatures of musical harmony. In May 1807, he was elected to the Accademia Italiana.

=100  \\$aMonsigny, Pierre-Alexandre$d1729-1817$4cmp$1http://www.wikidata.org/entity/Q705124$95419
=245  \\$aLe Déserteur.$bDrame en trois actes
=250  \\$a1st ed.

=500  \\$aPierre-Alexandre Monsigny (1729-1817) was a French composer and a member of the French Académie des Beaux-Arts (1813). He is considered, alongside André Grétry and François-André Danican Philidor, to have been the founder the opéra comique.
=500  \\$aLe déserteur (The Deserter) is a drame mélé de musique (opéra comique) by the French composer Pierre-Alexandre Monsigny with a libretto by Michel-Jean Sedaine. The work was Monsigny's greatest musical success and is one of the key operas of late 18th-century French opéra comique. The work mixes serious and comic elements, an example of the latter being the behaviour of the drunkard Montauciel. The theme of a last-minute reprieve from execution influenced later rescue opera. 
=534  \\$aIt was first performed on 6 March 1769 by the Comédie-Italienne at their public theatre, the Hôtel de Bourgogne in Paris.

=245  \\$aLe Droit du seigneur.$bComédie en trois actes et en prose

=500  \\$asee Map.004i for a selection of airs of this opera
=500  \\$aDroit du seigneur ('right of the lord'), also known as ius primae noctis ('right of the first night'), was a supposed legal right in medieval Europe, allowing feudal lords to have sexual relations with subordinate women, in particular, on the wedding nights of the women. Voltaire mentioned the practice in his Dictionnaire philosophique, published in 1764. He wrote the five-act comedy 'Le droit du seigneur' or 'L'écueil du sage' in 1762, although it was not performed until 1779, after his death. This play was the first time the term droit du seigneur was used.

=245  \\$aWerkstäte der heutigen Künste oder Die neue Kunsthistorie$nvol. 6
=250  \\$a1st ed.
=260  \\$aBrandenburg$aLeipzig$bHalle$c1779
=300  \\$a[193] pages$b6 folded, illustrated sheets inserted
=500  \\$aContains only pages page 215-408: the "Nachtrag zum Orgelbauer"
=500  \\$aHalle studied theology, philosophy and mathematics in Königsberg. In 1753, after completing his studies, he came to Berlin as an educator. There he was appointed to the Royal Prussian Cadet Corps (Corps des Cadets) in 1760 to take over the newly established professorship for history. He was the author of various scientific, technical/technological and historical (educational) books.

In his six-volume Werkstäte der heutigen Künste oder die neue Kunsthistorie, Halle describes the crafts of his time in great detail.

=100  \\$aHüllmandel, Nicolas-Joseph$d1756-1823$4cmp$1http://www.wikidata.org/entity/Q588375$97650
=245  \\$aI.er recueil de petits airs pour le clavecin ou piano forte op.2
=246  \1$aSix Divertimentos for the Harpsichord or Piano Forte
=260  \\$aParis$bs.n.$c17xx
=300  \\$a22 pages
=500  \\$aautograph signature
=500  \\$aAlso published in London ca 1776 as "Six Divertimentos for the Harpsichord or Piano Forte".
Digitalisation:
https://ks4.imslp.info/files/imglnks/usimg/d/d9/IMSLP659678-PMLP1046717-hullmandel_g.271.f.-7.-_Six_Divertimentos_for_the_Harpsichord_or_Piano_Forte.pdf
=500  \\$aBorn into a family of musicians, Hüllmandel began his musical studies with either Joseph Garnier or Franz Xaver Richter, or both of them, choirmasters at Strasbourg Cathedral. This is all that is known about his musical education. Fétis mentions that Hüllmandel studied with Carl Philipp Emanuel Bach, but this remains to be proven. Around the age of 20, Hüllmandel moved to Paris, where he met with immediate success in aristocratic circles and private salons, as the dedicatees of his first opuses attest: Marie-Antoinette, the Baroness Talleyrand and the Duc de Guines. He taught George Onslow and Hyacinthe Jadin. During the Revolution he moved to London, where he lived until his death. Hüllmandel composed 12 opus numbers, all for solo keyboard (harpsichord or fortepiano) or with ad libitum or obbligato accompaniment; these works were all published in Paris between 1773 and 1788, except for the last one, published in London in 1796. One wonders why he apparently stopped composing after this date. Hüllmandel also wrote the articles 'harpsichord' and 'fortepiano' for the Encyclopédie méthodique.

=100  \\$aSerre, Jean Adam$d1704-1788$4aut$97860
=245  \\$aEssais sur les principes de l'harmonie
=250  \\$a1st ed.
=260  \\$aParis$bPrault$c1753
=300  \\$a[viii]-206 pages
=500  \\$aPublished during the Querelle des Bouffons by a painter, physicist, chemist and musical theorist whom Burney met in Geneva
=500  \\$aSerre studied painting at the academy of Geneva, and at the university, after studying natural sciences, defended a thesis in physics under the direction of Jean-Louis Calandrini. He worked as a miniaturist in Marseille, Vienna and Paris, where he settled in 1751. He published several articles in the Mercure de France which he reused in his Essais sur les principes de l'harmonie in 1753, entering into debate with Charles-Henri Blainville, Rameau and Leonhard Euler. In 1756, he stayed in London and returned to Geneva where he published his Observations sur les principes de l'harmonie [...] in 1763: he challenged the musical theories developed by d'Alembert in the article "Fondamental" in the Encyclopédie, the 'Trattato di musica secondo la vera scienza dell'armonia' by Giuseppe Tartini and the 'Dictionaire harmonique' by Francesco Geminiani.
=500  \\$aIt was translated and commented on in German by Johann Adam Hiller in 1767 and quoted several times in Jean-Jacques Rousseau's Dictionnaire de musique.

=590  \\$aWelches die Melodien derer so wohl alten als neuen biß hieher eingeführten Gesänge unsers Teutschlandes in sich hält auch durch eine besondere Einrichtung dergestalt verfasset ist, daß diejenige Lieder, so man nicht zu singen gewußt, nunmehro mit ihren behörigen Melodien gesungen, und mit der Orgel oder Clavier accompagnirt werden können. =250  \\$a3rd rev. ed.

=336  \\$atext

=500  \\$aCited in Koopman 1985, 107
=500  \\$aTheoretical dictionary of the three fine arts of painting, sculpture and architecture as well as of poetry and music.
=500  \\$aTitle-page engraving by Daniel Chodowiecki  (1726-1801), German-Polish painter and printmaker. Allegory of the fine arts: the picture shows a light female figure surrounded by Minerva and the Graces. Minerva sits with lance and medusa shield. At her feet are tools for carving stone, a palette, brush, compass and square, masks and cothurn, a shawm and a plectrum. Minerva looks up at the female figure standing next to her, her gaze directed into the distance as if listening to an inner voice. A bright sun shines above the standing one. Minerva points with her hand to the instruments on the floor which refer to the three fine arts of painting, sculpture and architecture as well as to poetry and music.the three graces, meanwhile, are busy endowing the standing female figure with attributes that point to various arts. In the background, a landscape opens up in the depths, in which a naked, still uncivilised human family sits in front of a kind of primitive hut while one of them chases a deer. (Veronika Mertens, Die drei Grazien, Studien zu einem Bildmotiv in der Kunst der Neuzeit, Harrassowitz Verlag, 1994)
=534  \\$aOriginally published in 1771-74

=059  \\$aorg
=100  \\$aRinck, Christian Heinrich$d1770-1846$4cmp$1http://www.wikidata.org/entity/Q559451$96535
=245  \\$aNeues Choralbuch für das Großherzogthum Hessen
=260  \\$aOffenbach am Main$bAndré$c1814
=300  \\$axviii-100-xx pages$b16x23 cm, oblong
=336  \\$anotated music
=336  \\$aprinted
=500  \\$aorgan accompaniment for a collection of 138 chorales
=500  \\$aRinck comes from a family of teachers. From 1786, he received organ and composition lessons from a pupil of Johann Sebastian Bach, by Johann Christian Kittel (1732-1809) in Erfurt. In 1805 he moved to Darmstadt and become cantor and organist at the city church. Later he was employed as court organist and chamber musician of Grand Duke Louis I of Hesse-Darmstadt. 
Rinck was known early on as an excellent organist and was much in demand as an expert.His organ compositions were highly appreciated and his "Praktische Orgelschule", op. 55 was a leading method in Germany until the 20th century. Rinck made an important contribution to the renewal and improvement of Protestant organ music at the beginning of the 19th century.

=500  \\$aDavid F. Faßmann (1685-1744) was a popular journalist, a member of the tobacco college and historiographer
=501  \\$aFaßmann's 'Die neu-entdeckten Elisäischen Felder' (1735)
=590  \\$aOder gantz natürliche Abbildung solcher Gelehrten, die da vermeynen alle Gelehrsamkeit und Wissenschafften verschlucket zu haben, auch in dem Wahn stehen, daß ihres gleichen nicht auf Erden zu finden, wannenhero sie alle andere Menschen gegen sich verachten, einen unerträglichen Stoltz und Hochmuth von sich spüren lassen; in der That aber doch selber so, wie sie in ihrer Haut stecken, Ignoranten, Pedanten, ja Ertz-Fantasten und tumme Sympel sind, die von der wahren Gelehrsamkeit, womit die Weisheit verknüpffet seyn muß, weit entfernet. Nebst einer lustigen Dedication und sonderbaren Vorrede. Dergleichen verkehrten Gelehrten zur guten Lehre, und verhoffentlich daraus fliessenden Besserung; andern aber, so sich denen Studiis widmen, und noch Anfänger sind, zur getreuen Warnung, auch sonst jederman zum Vergnügen geschrieben

=041  \\$adut
=100  \\$aHuygens, Constantijn$d1596-1687$4aut$1http://www.wikidata.org/entity/Q560746$95174
=245  \\$aBatava Tempe:$b't Voor-hout van 's Graven-Hage
=260  \\$aMiddelburg$bVan der Hellen$bVan de Venne$c1622
=300  \\$a31pages$billustrations
=500  \\$aOne of the two collections with which Constantijn Huygens (1596-1687) broke through as a poet
=500  \\$a2 remarkable engravings included: title page (elaborate printers-logo) and first page (town-view of the Voorhout square in The Hague).
=501  \\$aBound in with 'Kerkuraia mastix' and 'Groete aen de ioffrouwen'
=520  \\$aThe title of this great work of poetry, 'Batava Tempe', an ode to a beautiful and famous street in the old city centre of The Hague, the Lange Voorhout, accurately conveys the content. The word Tempe is derived from a beautiful valley in northern Greece, Thessaly to be precise, which was so called in antiquity. Apparently Huygens relates this beautiful valley to the Voorhout in The Hague. So the poem is about the Voorhout, which is also called Batave Tempe and is located in The Hague. Constantijn Huygens could also have chosen another place to write a great poem about, but apparently the Voorhout surpassed all other places and played the most important role for him in his life.
=534  \\$aOriginally published in 1621
=590  \\$aPoëtelick aff-ghemaelt door Constantin Huygens
=648  \0$a17th Century (1601-1700)$1http://www.wikidata.org/entity/Q7016$920923

=041  \\$adut
=100  \\$aHuygens, Constantijn$d1596-1687$4aut$1http://www.wikidata.org/entity/Q560746$95174
=245  \\$aGroete aen de ioffrouwen Anna ende Maria Tesselschade Visschers, mitsgaders de Heere P. C. Hooft Drost van Muyden
=246  \1$aVan over 't Noorder Nauw
=250  \\$a1st ed.
=260  \\$aMiddelburg$bVan der Hellen & Van de Venne$c1622

=100  \\$aZehentner, Paul$d1589-1648$4aut$1http://www.wikidata.org/entity/Q55874362$97979
=245  \\$aPromontorium malæ spei: impiis periculose navigantibus propositum
=250  \\$a1st ed.
=260  \\$aHaupt; Widmanstadt$bGraz$c1643
=300  \\$a[xxxviii]-752-[10] pages$bgilt edges, 2 engravings
=336  \\$abook
=336  \\$aprinted
=500  \\$aJesuit warning of the consequences of licentiousness ("Promontory, thoughts of hope for the wicked goal that sailed dangerously. Whether it is a sign of rejection and note: procrastination of repentance written precautionary men's amendment is reluctance, sometimes hope to repent.")
=500  \\$aFirst and only edition of a Latin edifying text on moral and religious issues by the Jesuit Paul Zehentner (1589-1648), preacher at the Graz court of the widow of the Holy Roman Emperor Ferdinand II and teacher of grammar, the humanities and the Holy Scripture at Millestadt in Austria. A moral-theological treatment of state theory, astrology and magic, intended to highlight the dangers of licentious behaviour. 
=500  \\$aIt provides our first known reference to the tragedy of Leontius, a play Zehentner saw at the Jesuit University in Ingolstadt in 1615, and which was to serve as a prototype for the Don Juan legend (Keefe, Mozart studies, p. 140). 
=500  \\$aZehentner dedicated the book to Leonardus Helfridus, Count at Maggau, 26 October 1643, and received a privilege from the Holy Roman Emperor Ferdinand III.
=500  \\$aEngraved allegorical frontispiece and a richly designed armorial and emblematic dedication plate, both by David Tscherning.

=500  \\$aIn 1822 Logier was called to Berlin to help found a music academy, and subsequently trained elementary teachers on behalf of the king until 1826. In addition, the publishing house of his brother Wilhelm published his textbooks in German. =260  \\$aLondon$bAstorga$c1768
=500  \\$aJuan (or Jean) Oliver Astorga (1733-1830) was a Spanish violinist, flautist and composer. He was one of the most important musicians of Spanish classicism, unfortunately now little known and studied. He led an itinerant life in various European cities and courts, which allowed him to get first-hand knowledge of the music being practised in the most cosmopolitan and advanced environments of his time, before his return to Spain.

=100  \\$aDuni, Egidio$d1708-1775$4cmp$1http://www.wikidata.org/entity/Q953519$95418
=245  \\$aLe Peintre amoureux de son modéle.$bOpéra-comique en 2 actes mêlé d'ariettes
=260  \\$aParis$bDuni$c1758
=300  \\$a[ii]-97-[1]-4-17 pages
=500  \\$aUnder Goldoni's influence, Duni made contact with the director of the Opéra-comique in Paris, Jean Monnet. At first, Monnet was not very enthusiastic about the idea of entrusting the composition of a French opera to an Italian composer, but then he agreed and suggested a text by Louis Anseaume: Le Peintre amoureux de son modèle. The resulting opéra comique by Duni was premiered in July 1757 with brilliant success. The composer then moved permanently to Paris, where he remained until his death.

=500  \\$aPreface: "The Editor offers to the public a new edition of Beethoven's NineSymphonies in full score, prepared with the most scrupulous care and the labour of years, in the hope of producing something which by intrinsic correctness and external elegance might be found not unworthy of those immortal works. The clear engraving and spelndid printing are the result of a new process, now successfully executed for the first time in England. The price is nevertheless even lower than that of the poorest and least careful of the former editions. The Editor ventures to issue them at this price, solely in the hope of thereby rendering these glorious masterpieces accessible to all, as a welcome companion in the concert-room, and a treasure and ornament for the home."

=100  \\$aJunck, Heinrich Gotthilf$4asn$98007
=245  \\$aWendisches Choral-Buch
=260  \\$as.l.$cs.d.
=300  \\$a163 pages
=500  \\$aCarefully written music manuscript containing eighteen two- to four-part hymns in Wendish and twenty-one in German. Passion chorales at the end, some with more than thirty verses. In some cases the composers are specified. A valuable source on church music in Lusatia around the middle of the eighteenth century.
=500  \\$aLusatia (German: Lausitz), also known as Sorbia, is a historical region in Central Europe, split between Germany and Poland. 
=500  \\$aHistorically the Sorbian languages have also been known as Wendish (named after the Wends, the earliest Slavic people in modern Poland and Germany) or Lusatian.

=260  \\$aBrussels$aParis$bYpen, van; Mechtler$bCornouaille$cs.d.
=300  \\$a11 pages
=500  \\$aLoose kbd part
=500  \\$aFerdinand was the son of Guillaume Staes, organist at the Brussels royal chapel. From 1758, Ferdinand Staes had lessons from his father and later from Ignaz Vitzthumb. He worked as harpsichordist at the Théâtre de la Monnaie in Brussels. In 1767, he was appointed assistant to his father (second organist at the royal chapel). In 1772, Ferdinand Staes became organist at the Madeleine church in Brussels.
